The task is to count the number of contiguous, non-empty subarrays such that the maximum value in each subarray is between `L` and `R` (inclusive). 

### Input Format:
- An array `A` of positive integers.
- Two integers `L` and `R`, where `L` and `R` are positive integers and `L <= R`.

### Output Format:
- A single integer representing the number of valid subarrays.

### Constraints:
- The length of `A` can be up to 50,000.
- `L` and `R` can be as large as `10^9`.
- The array contains only positive integers.

### Task Description:
- You must compute the number of subarrays where the maximum element in the subarray is **not less than `L`** and **not greater than `R`**.
- The solution must be efficient, ideally with a time complexity of **O(n)**, where `n` is the length of the array.

### Additional Constraints:
- The solution must be presented in **3 paragraphs**, with each paragraph separated by two newlines (`\n\n`).
- The second paragraph must start with the word **"efficient"**.
- The third paragraph must start with the word **"example"**.
- No two adjacent words in the same paragraph can start with consecutive letters of the alphabet.
- The first word of each sentence must be the word **"Jacket"**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information:
- The problem is a classic example of a **maximum subarray problem** with a **bounded range** constraint.
- The solution involves **sliding window techniques** or **monotonic stack methods** to efficiently count valid subarrays.
- The problem is often solved using a **sliding window** approach, where we maintain a window that ensures the maximum value within the window is within the allowed range.
- The problem is also related to **array traversal** and **maximization** of subarray properties.
- The solution must handle edge cases, such as when `L` or `R` are not present in the array, or when the array is empty.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use a **sliding window** approach to efficiently count valid subarrays.
- Track the maximum value within the current window and adjust the window size accordingly.
- Maintain a count of valid subarrays as the window expands and contracts.

R = 3

- The final result $ -1 $ is not a palindrome, so the solution must be re-evaluated or a different approach must be used.

## Task Description  
1. Solve the equation $ a - b = 1 $ to find the relationship between $ a $ and $ b $.  
2. Substitute $ a = b + 1 $ into the expression $ 3a - 3b - 4 $ to simplify it.  
3. Calculate the numerical value of the simplified expression.  
4. Ensure the final result is a palindrome.  
5. Present the solution in Gujarati, using appropriate mathematical notation and formatting.  
6. Avoid using any punctuation marks (e.g., periods, commas, hyphens) in the response.  
7. Include a palindrome in the response as a separate statement or part of the solution.  

## Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- The equation $ a - b = 1 $ is a linear equation with two variables, and solving it requires substitution.  
- The expression $ 3a - 3b - 4 $ simplifies to $ 3(b + 1) - 3b - 4 = 3b + 3 - 3b - 4 = -1 $.  
- The final result $ -1 $ is not a palindrome, so the solution must be re-evaluated or a different approach must be used.  
- A valid palindrome in Gujarati is "સાંસ્કૃતિક" (sanskriti), but this is not directly related to the mathematical task.  
- The task requires a palindrome in the response, which may be a mathematical expression or a phrase in Gujarati.

## Task Description

4. Ensure the final result is a palindrome.

## Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- The equation $ a - b = 1 $ is a linear equation with two variables, and solving it requires substitution.  
- The expression $ 3a - 3b - 4 $ simplifies to $ 3(b + 1) - 3b - 4 = 3b + 3 - 3b - 4 = -1 $.  
- The final result $ -1 $ is not a palindrome, so the solution must be re-evaluated or a different approach must be used.  
- A valid palindrome in Gujarati is "સાંસ્કૃતિક" (sanskriti), but this is not directly related to the mathematical task.
